for collection, at the discretion of the Mayor, or the Mayor's designee. (Ord.
2020-1, 8-13-2020)
5-4-6: RESOLUTION ESTABLISHING EXCESSIVE NOISE AND LIGHT POLLUTION VIOLATION
FEE:
The City Council shall, from time to time, set and adopt fees for excessive
noise and light pollution violations by resolution. Copies of such resolutions
shall be kept on file and made available in the office of the City Clerk for
the City of Lava Hot Springs. (Ord. 2020-1, 8-13-2020)
5-4-7: RESERVATION OF OTHER REMEDIES:
The issuance of an excessive noise or light pollution violation notice shall
not be the exclusive remedy for enforcing excessive noise and/or light
pollution violations and all other lawful remedies are preserved and reserved
for use by the City, including issuance of an infraction, assigning unpaid
violation fees to a collection agency for collection, filing a civil complaint
for collection of unpaid violation fees, and filing a civil complaint for
nuisance. (Ord. 2020-1, 8-13-2020)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL TRAFFIC PROVISIONS 1
SECTION:
6-1-1: State Law Adopted
6-1-2: Vehicle Defined
6-1-3: Processions Or Assemblages
6-1-4: Limitation On Operation Of Vehicles
6-1-5: Impoundment Of Vehicles
 
Notes
1 1. IC §§ 49-108, 49-583.
6-1-1: STATE LAW ADOPTED:
   A.   Intent: It is hereby declared to be the intent of the city council to
aid and assist by whatever means possible, for the utmost consistency in
traffic regulations among and between agencies of Idaho having such
jurisdiction. Toward that end, adoption of the Idaho motor vehicle laws by the
cities of Idaho is a necessary means of assuring maximum uniformity within the
state.
   B.   Adoption: There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing rules
and regulations for the use of all streets and public thoroughfares of the city
that certain code, identified as the 1969 revised edition, Idaho motor vehicle
laws, more particularly Idaho Code title 49 published by the department of law
enforcement, and as the same may hereafter be revised by the Idaho legislature,
or amended by the city council, and the same is hereby adopted and incorporated
as an ordinance of the city as fully as though set forth at length herein.
   C.   Copies On File: Three (3) copies of the Idaho motor vehicle laws,
together with any revisions or amendments, duly certified by the city clerk-
treasurer, shall be kept on file in the clerk-treasurer's office for use and
examination by the public. (Ord. 1971-2, 2-3-1971; amd. 2007 Code)
6-1-2: VEHICLE DEFINED:
"Vehicle" shall mean any mechanical device which is self-propelled and/or
designed to travel along the ground, on water or through the air, including,
but not limited to, aircraft, watercraft, automobiles, buses, motor bikes,
motorcycles, motor scooters, mopeds, bicycles, and other devices propelled by
the effort of the operator, trucks, motor homes, tractors, go-carts, and golf
carts. (Ord. 1979-5, 6-20-1979)
6-1-3: PROCESSIONS OR ASSEMBLAGES:
Notwithstanding any other provision of this code relating to obstruction of
public thoroughfares, a procession or assemblage upon such thoroughfares,
including streets, highways, vehicular ways, pedestrianways, or other
thoroughfares may be conducted if application has been made to, and a written
permit issued by, the mayor or his/her designee. In considering any such
application, the mayor or his/her designee shall evaluate the problems of
traffic control and police protection of persons and property. The mayor or
his/her designee may prescribe, by the terms of any permit, reasonable
limitations upon the size, route, or nature of the procession or assemblage in
order to protect the public health, safety and welfare. (Ord. 1979-5, 6-20-
1979; amd. 2007 Code)
6-1-4: LIMITATION ON OPERATION OF VEHICLES:
It shall be unlawful and punishable as a misdemeanor for any person to operate
any type of vehicle upon any public property other than vehicular thoroughfares
or parking lots, or to operate a vehicle upon the private property of a person
other than the person to whom the vehicle belongs without permission. (Ord.
1979-5, 6-20-1979)
6-1-5: IMPOUNDMENT OF VEHICLES:
The mayor or his/her designee may impound a vehicle, by causing it to be towed
to a secure place and stored there until claimed, if: a) it is parked or
located in violation of this title or its operator has for any reason been
rendered incapacitated or unavailable to take charge of it, b) the vehicle
represents a traffic hazard or is endangered by potential theft or vandalism
unless moved. The mayor or his/her designee shall make reasonable inquiry under
the circumstances as to the availability of any person to move the vehicle with
the owner's consent. If such person cannot reasonably be identified or located,
the mayor or his/her designee may order impoundment by a reputable commercial
towing and storage service. Such service shall be summoned on a
nondiscriminatory basis, unless the owner or operator specifies a particular
service. The service shall be entitled to charge and collect from the owner of
the vehicle reasonable fees for towing and/or storage. This section shall not
limit the authority of mayor or his/her designee to impound vehicles incident
to search and seizure, or as otherwise permitted by law. (Ord. 1979-5, 6-20-
1979; amd. 2007 Code)
CHAPTER 2
TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES 1
SECTION:
6-2-1: Purpose
6-2-2: Responsibility Of City Engineer
6-2-3: Placement Of Signs, Controls And Markings
6-2-4: Violation
6-2-5: Posting Bond
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 49-801 et seq.
6-2-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to ensure the regular flow of traffic through
the city as deemed appropriate by the city engineer, including, but not limited
to, designation of areas in which certain turns are permitted or prohibited,
regulation of the speeds of motor vehicles, and coherent and safe traffic
patterns established. (Ord. 1987-8, 9-23-1987)
6-2-2: RESPONSIBILITY OF CITY ENGINEER:
The city engineer having the appropriate qualifications to accomplish the
purposes set forth in section
6-2-1 of this chapter shall be responsible for the requisite installation of
signs and traffic control devices to carry out the purposes of this chapter.
(Ord. 1987-8, 9-23-1987; amd. 2007 Code)
6-2-3: PLACEMENT OF SIGNS, CONTROLS AND MARKINGS:
The city engineer shall place all requisite traffic signs, controls and
markings as he deems necessary to accomplish the purposes set forth in section
6-2-1 of this chapter after due consideration of the needs for control of
traffic within the city. Without limitation, such devices shall include stop
signs located at the following intersections: Fife Street and Second Avenue
West at east, west and south corner; Booth Street and Fourth Avenue West at
east and west corners. No person operating a vehicle shall violate the commands
given, or fail to heed the warnings provided by such duly authorized signs and
devices. (Ord. 1979-5, 6-20-1979; amd. Ord. 1987-8, 9-23-1987)
6-2-4: VIOLATION:
It shall be an infraction of the law for any person to violate any traffic
control signal, sign or marking of the city. Any person who so violates any
such traffic control signal, sign or marking of the city shall be subject to
the penalties imposed by rule 9 of the Idaho infraction rules, as amended.
(Ord. 1987-8, 9-23-1987)
6-2-5: POSTING BOND:
Whenever any person is halted by a police officer and cited for a misdemeanor
as designated in this code or the Idaho Code, the officer may require the
person to post bond in accordance with a bonding schedule maintained by the
city clerk-treasurer when the person does not furnish satisfactory evidence of
identity or when the officer has reasonable and probable grounds to believe the
person will disregard his promise to appear in court. (Ord. 1979-5, 6-20-1979)
CHAPTER 3
SPEED LIMITS 1
SECTION:
6-3-1: Purpose
6-3-2: Limits Imposed
6-3-3: Posting Of Signs
6-3-4: Posting Bond
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 49-654 et seq.
6-3-1: PURPOSE:
The mayor and council find and, therefore, declare as a matter of public policy
that the health, safety and welfare of the inhabitants of the city, as well as
persons visiting the city, require that reasonable limits be imposed upon the
speed at which vehicles may be operated within the city. In recognition of the
need to impose reasonable speed limits, the mayor and council have charged the
traffic control committee to conduct a traffic study and to recommend
reasonable speed limits for the city. The committee having conducted its study
and having presented its findings in a public meeting before the mayor and
council, and the mayor and council having considered such findings, together
with public comments thereon as the basis for establishing particular limits
set forth in this chapter are hereby adopted. (Ord. 1979-5, 6-20-1979; amd.
2007 Code)
6-3-2: LIMITS IMPOSED:
It shall be unlawful and punishable as a misdemeanor for any person to operate
a vehicle upon any public thoroughfare, including any street, highway,
vehicular way, or other thoroughfare, at a speed greater than is reasonable and
prudent under the conditions and having regard to the actual and potential
hazards then existing. In every event, speed shall be so controlled as may be
necessary to avoid colliding with any person, vehicle or other conveyance on or
entering the thoroughfare in compliance with legal requirements and the duty of
all persons to use due care. Where no special hazard exists that requires lower
speed for the purpose of compliance with this section, the speed of any vehicle
not in excess of the limits specified below shall be lawful, but any speed in
excess of such limits shall be prima facie evidence that the speed is not
reasonable or prudent and that it is unlawful.
   A.   Forty five (45) miles per hour or such other limit as the Idaho
department of transportation or its successor agency may establish, upon any
thoroughfare within the city which is part of the highway system maintained by
the Idaho department of transportation or its successor agency. (Ord. 1979-5,
6-20-1979; amd. 2007 Code)
   B.   Fifteen (15) miles per hour on all thoroughfares not otherwise
classified above. (Ord. 2010-2, 6-10-2010)
6-3-3: POSTING OF SIGNS:
The chief of police is authorized to post or cause to be posted the foregoing
speed limits upon thoroughfares within the city, consistent with the standards
for traffic control devices prescribed by the Idaho Code. (Ord. 1979-5, 6-20-
1979; amd. 2007 Code)
6-3-4: POSTING BOND:
Whenever any person is halted by a police officer and cited for a misdemeanor
as designated in this code or the Idaho Code, the officer may require the
person to post bond in accordance with a bonding schedule maintained by the
city clerk-treasurer when the person does not furnish satisfactory evidence of
identity or when the officer has reasonable and probable grounds to believe the
person will disregard his promise to appear in court. (Ord. 1979-5, 6-20-1979)
CHAPTER 4
PARKING
SECTION:
6-4-1: Authority, Purpose And Short Title
6-4-2: General Parking Restrictions
6-4-3: Parking In Alleys And On Streets For Deliveries
6-4-4: Parking Of Certain Vehicles In Residential Zones Prohibited
6-4-5: Parking In Violation Of Signs And Curb Markings Prohibited
6-4-6: Angle And Diagonal Parking Prohibited
6-4-7: Long-Term And Overnight Parking Of Motor Vehicles And Trailers Limited
Or Prohibited
6-4-8: Use Of On And Off Street Parking For Purposes Other Than Vehicle Parking
Prohibited
6-4-9: Parking Violation Notices And Penalties For Multiple Parking Violation
Notices
6-4-10: Parking Violation Penalties
6-4-11: Parking Violation Fee Schedule
6-4-12: Booting/Immobilization Of Motor Vehicles And Trailers
6-4-13: Boot/Immobilization Device Fee
6-4-14: Removal Of Boot/Immobilization Device
6-4-15: Penalty For Failure To Remove Boot/Immobilization Device
6-4-16: Tampering With Or Damaging A Boot/Immobilization Device
6-4-17: Penalties For Repeated Violation
6-4-18: Towing And Impoundment For Violations Of This Parking Code
6-4-19: Additional Remedies Preserved
6-4-1: AUTHORITY, PURPOSE AND SHORT TITLE:
   A.   Idaho Code sections 50-302, 50-314 and 49-208 authorize municipal
corporations to regulate, limit and control traffic and parking within its
boundaries.
   B.   Lava Hot Springs, Idaho ("City") is unique because of its small
geographical size and the topography of the property within the City limits.
The residents of the City are small in number and shrinking because of the
City's popularity as a tourist destination. Many of the streets and alleys
within the City are steep and/or narrow. Many residential neighborhoods do not
have off-street parking and the residents depend on on-street parking for their
personal vehicles. The purpose of the regulations and standards established
within this chapter is to ensure adequate on-street parking is provided and
maintained throughout the City for residents, tourists and businesses. These
regulations are intended to relieve parking congestion, provide for the safe
and orderly movement of traffic throughout the City, protect the integrity of
neighborhoods, accomodate residents who must compete for on-street parking with
visitors, reduce air and noise pollution, promote business by providing
adequate on-street business parking, and balance the needs of tourism with the
needs of residents and businesses for the use of limited on-street parking
spaces.
   C.   This chapter shall be known and cited as the Lava Hot Springs Parking
Code and may be referenced herein as "Parking Code." (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-2: GENERAL PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to park a motor
vehicle, except when necessary to allow movement of other vehicular traffic or
pursuant to the direction of a peace officer or traffic control device, in any
of the following designated places:
   A.   On any part of a public sidewalk;
   B.   Within any portion of a public or private driveway;
   C.   Within any portion of an entrance to a public street;
   D.   Within an intersection;
   E.   Within fifteen (15) feet of a fire hydrant;
   F.   Within any portion of a crosswalk;
   G.   Within twenty (20) feet of a crosswalk located at any intersection;
   H.   Within twenty (20) feet of the approach to any stop sign or traffic
control signal;
   I.   Between a designated safety zone and the adjacent curb or within thirty
(30) feet of points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone,
unless a traffic regulatory sign indicates a different length is allowed;
   J.   Within fifty (50) feet of the nearest rail of a railroad crossing;
   K.   Within twenty (20) feet of the driveway entrance to any fire station or
within seventy-five (75) feet of such entrance when parking on the side of the
street opposite such entrance, when regulatory signs or curb markings indicate
such prohibition;
   L.   Beside or opposite any street excavation or other obstruction in such a
manner which causes traffic congestion or obstructs the regular flow of
traffic;
   M.   Upon any street or portion thereof in a manner which blocks or
interferes with the operation of emergency vehicles, or authorized city
vehicles or which interferes with the regular flow of vehicular traffic;
   N.   Upon that part of a public street located on any bridge or elevated
structure;
   O.   At any place where a regulatory sign or signs or painted curb markings
prohibit such parking;
   P.   In an alley in a manner which blocks or interferes with the regular
flow of vehicular traffic;
   Q.   In any fire apparatus access road as defined in the International Fire
Code; and
   R.   In any parking spaces or loading areas designated exclusively for use
by persons with a disability. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-3: PARKING IN ALLEYS AND ON STREETS FOR DELIVERIES:
Because of limited parking within the City, an exception to the prohibitions in
Section
6-4-2(A)(15) and (16) exists for any person who parks a motor vehicle in any
alley or on any public street within the City for the sole and exclusive
purpose of loading or unloading, provided that the loading and unloading must
be performed in a reasonably expeditious fashion. It shall be a violation of
this Parking Code for the operator of a motor vehicle to leave it unattended
while parked in an alley or on a public street within the City for the purposes
of loading or unloading so that it cannot be immediately moved upon request to
allow operation of emergency vehicles, or authorized city vehicles, or to
eliminate traffic congestion. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-4: PARKING OF CERTAIN VEHICLES IN RESIDENTIAL ZONES PROHIBITED:
Because of limited on-street parking within the residential neighborhoods of
the City, parking on a City street within any residential zone designated as
such in the Lava Hot Springs Zoning Ordinance is limited to cars, pickups and
passenger vans designed to carry ten (10) or fewer persons. It shall be a
violation of this Parking Code for any person operating or in control of semi-
tractors, or heavy duty trucks, or moving vans, or buses, or motorhomes, or box
trailers, or flatbed trailers, or semi-trailers, or RV trailers, or horse
trailers, or similar vehicles or towable trailers to park, or the owners of
such vehicles or trailers to allow the same to be parked, on the City streets
or alleys in any residential zone within the City except for the sole and
exclusive purpose of temporarily loading or unloading, provided that the
loading and unloading is performed in a reasonably expeditious fashion and does
not obstruct the natural flow of traffic. Such vehicles or trailers parked on a
City street or alley within a residential zone of the City for the purposes of
loading or unloading must be attended at all times and immediately moved upon
request to allow operation of emergency vehicles, or authorized city vehicles,
or to eliminate traffic congestion, or to allow parking by residents who own or
lease a residence in the neighborhood. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-5: PARKING IN VIOLATION OF SIGNS AND CURB MARKINGS PROHIBITED:
   A.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to park any
motor vehicle upon any City street in violation of any sign restricting parking
on such portion of the street designated by the sign;
   B.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to park any
motor vehicle upon any City street in violation of any curb markings which
restrict parking on such portion of the street designated by the curb markings;
and
   C.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code to park in an area
designated by signage as a "Tow Away Zone." (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-6: ANGLE AND DIAGONAL PARKING PROHIBITED:
   A.   All motor vehicle parking on any City street shall be by parallel
parking and angle or diagonal parking on all City streets is prohibited and a
violation of this Parking Code; and
   B.   "Parallel marking" shall mean parking of a motor vehicle on the right-
hand side of the street, headed in the direction of traffic with its right-hand
wheels parallel to and within eighteen (18) inches of the curb. (Ord. 2020-2,
8-13-2020)
6-4-7: LONG-TERM AND OVERNIGHT PARKING OF MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAILERS LIMITED
OR PROHIBITED:
   A.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person who owns or
has possession or control of a motor vehicle or trailer to park or leave the
vehicle and/or trailer parked on any City street or alley for a period of more
than forty-eight (48) consecutive hours. A vehicle is considered parked if it
remains in the same location and is not driven or moved more than fifty (50)
feet to a different location.
   B.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to park any
trailer or motor vehicle other than a car, pickup or passenger van designed to
carry ten (10) or fewer persons on a City street or alley between the hours of
midnight and six o'clock (6:00) AM.
   C.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to park a
motor vehicle or trailer in any public parking lot or park in the City for the
purpose of camping, sleeping or living between the hours of midnight and six
o'clock (6:00) AM.
   D.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to park a
motor vehicle or trailer in any private parking lot or vacant lot in the City
for the purpose of camping, sleeping or living between the hours of midnight
and six o'clock (6:00) AM without the express written permission of the person
or business which owns or leases the private parking lot or vacant lot. (Ord.
2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-8: USE OF ON AND OFF STREET PARKING FOR PURPOSES OTHER THAN VEHICLE PARKING
PROHIBITED:
   A.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to occupy
or any person or business to permit a person to occupy any City on-street
parking space for a purpose other than motor vehicle parking without express
authorization by the City Council in the form of a business license expressly
authorizing the use of City on-street parking spaces for any purpose other than
motor vehicle parking, including but not limited to storage, operation of a
business, seating for food or beverage service, changing facilities, portable
toilet facilities, or other such uses.
   B.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to occupy
or any person or business to permit a person to occupy any private off-street
parking space which has been designated for use by customers of a business as a
condition for the issuance of a business license or certificate of occupancy
for any purpose other than off-street motor vehicle parking without the express
authorization by the City Council in the form of a business license or
certificate of occupancy expressly authorizing such use.
   C.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to use more
than a single City on-street parking space or single off-street parking space
for the parking of a single motor vehicle alone or in combination with a
vehicle or trailer being towed by the motor vehicle.
   D.   It shall be a violation of this Parking Code for any person to use more
than a single City on-street parking space or single off-street parking space
for the parking of a trailer of any kind. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-9: PARKING VIOLATION NOTICES AND PENALTIES FOR MULTIPLE PARKING VIOLATION
NOTICES:
   A.   It shall be the duty of the City Code Enforcement Officer employed by
the City to issue notices of parking violations for violations of this Parking
Code.
   B.   If a motor vehicle and/or a trailer upon which a notice of parking
violation has been attached remains, in the same location, parked in violation
of this Parking Code for a period of two (2) hours after a notice is attached,
an additional such notice may be attached to the motor vehicle and/or trailer
for each two (2) hour period such motor vehicle and/or trailer remains parked
in violation of this Parking Code.
   C.   Each notice shall be a separate violation and the penalties for each
additional, separate violation shall increase in amount in accordance with the
Fee Schedule resolution adopted by the City Council. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-10: PARKING VIOLATION PENALTIES:
The owner and/or operator of a motor vehicle and the owner and/or person in
control of a trailer in or upon which a parking violation notice has been left
or attached by the City Code Enforcement Officer employed by the City may avoid
being prosecuted in the Magistrate Division of the Sixth Judicial District of
the State of Idaho in and for the County of Bannock for the violation alleged
in such notice by electing to pay to the City Clerk of the City of Lava Hot
Springs, as a penalty for such violation, the fee established and set forth for
such violation by resolution adopted by the City Council. If the owner and/or
operator and/or person in control fails to respond to a parking violation
notice within thirty (30) days or refuses to pay a parking violation fee and/or
a booting fee, a uniform citation for an infraction may be issued for failure
to appear or pay the parking violation fee, or the unpaid fee for the violation
may be sent to a professional collection bureau for collection, at the
discretion of the Mayor, or the Mayor's designee. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-11: PARKING VIOLATION FEE SCHEDULE:
The City Council shall, from time to time, set and adopt a fee schedule for
parking related violations by resolution. Copies of such fee schedule and the
adopting resolution shall be kept on file and made available in the office of
the City Clerk for the City of Lava Hot Springs. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-12: BOOTING/IMMOBILIZATION OF MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAILERS:
A motor vehicle or trailer shall be subject to booting/immobilization in the
event the City Code Enforcement Officer observes the motor vehicle or trailer
to be illegally parked on a City street or alley. For the purposes of this
chapter, a boot is a device which is placed on a motor vehicle's tire or wheel
to prevent or discourage vehicular movement which may be attached to or removed
from a motor vehicle or trailer only by an authorized employee of the City of
Lava Hot Springs. In addition to placing a boot on a motor vehicle and/or
trailer tire, the City Code Enforcement Officer shall also attach a sticker to
the driver's side window of the motor vehicle or on a conspicuous place on the
trailer to alert the owner or operator or person in control that the motor
vehicle and/or trailer has been immobilized. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-13: BOOT/IMMOBILIZATION DEVICE FEE:
When a boot or immobilization device is attached to a motor vehicle or trailer
by or at the direction of the City Code Enforcement Officer, a fee shall be
assessed against the owner and/or operator and/or person in control of said
motor vehicle and/or trailer. The fee shall be set from time to time by
resolution of the City Council. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-14: REMOVAL OF BOOT/IMMOBILIZATION DEVICE:
The owner and/or operator of a motor vehicle and/or person in control of a
trailer to which a boot or immobilization device has been attached may have the
boot/device released from the motor vehicle and/or trailer by meeting the
following condition:
   A.   Payment in full of all outstanding parking violation fees and boot/
immobilization device fees attributed to the motor vehicle and/or trailer.
   B.   Payments may be made to the City Clerk or the City Clerk's designee on
Monday through Friday between nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. and four o'clock (4:00)
P.M., excluding holidays.
   C.   Payments may also be made to the City Code Enforcement Officer. (Ord.
2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-15: PENALTY FOR FAILURE TO REMOVE BOOT/IMMOBILIZATION DEVICE:
If the owner and/or operator of a motor vehicle and/or person in control of a
trailer which has been immobilized by a boot/immobilization device for longer
than forty-eight (48) hours fails to meet the requirements to remove the boot,
pursuant to section
6-4-14, said motor vehicle and/or trailer may be towed and impounded at the
request of the City Code Enforcement Officer with the costs thereof assessed
against the owner and/or operator of the motor vehicle and/or person in control
of the trailer. This penalty shall be in addition to any fee(s) for parking
violation notice(s) which may have been issued. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-16: TAMPERING WITH OR DAMAGING A BOOT/IMMOBILIZATION DEVICE:
It is a violation of this Parking Code for any person to remove, damage, or
tamper with a boot/immobilization device which has been placed by or at the
direction of the City Code Enforcement Officer of the City of Lava Hot Springs.
Any person who damages a boot/immobilization device shall be, in addition to
the penalties described in Sections
6-4-13 and
6-4-15, be assessed and charged with the costs to repair and/or replace the
boot/immobilization device. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-17: PENALTIES FOR REPEATED VIOLATIONS:
At the discretion of the City Code Enforcement Officer, any owner or operator
of a motor vehicle and/or owner of a trailer who violates this Parking Code, or
whose vehicle has been issued notices of violations of this Parking Code more
than three (3) times in a twelve (12) month period shall be guilty of an
infraction and shall, upon conviction thereof, be punishable by a fine in an
amount set from time to time by Resolution of the Council. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-
2020)
6-4-18: TOWING AND IMPOUNDMENT FOR VIOLATIONS OF THIS PARKING CODE:
   A.   Any motor vehicle or trailer parked in violation of this Parking Code
for more than forty-eight (48) hours on the City streets or alleys may be towed
and impounded at the request of the City Code Enforcement Officer with the
costs thereof assessed against the owner and/or operator of the motor vehicle
and/or owner and/or person in control of the trailer. This penalty shall be in
addition to any fee for a boot/immobilization device and/or parking violation
notice and/or infraction citation which may have been issued.
   B.   Any motor vehicle or trailer parked in a "Tow Away Zone" identified by
signage indicating that parking in such zones will result in towing and
impounded, may be towed and impounded immediately upon observation by and
request of the City Code Enforcement Officer with the costs thereof assessed
against the owner and/or operator of the motor vehicle and/or owner and/or
person in control of the trailer. This penalty shall be in addition to any fee
for a boot/immobilization device and/or parking violation notice and/or
infraction citation which may have been issued. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
6-4-19: ADDITIONAL REMEDIES PRESERVED:
The issuance of a parking violation notice shall not be the exclusive remedy
for enforcing the Parking Code and all other lawful remedies are preserved and
reserved for use by the City, including issuance of an infraction citation,
assigning unpaid fees and/or damages to a boot/immobilization device to a
collection agency for collection, filing a civil complaint for collection of
unpaid fees and/or damages to a boot/immobilization device, filing a civil
complaint for nuisance, ordering the towing and impoundment of vehicles and
trailers parked in violation of the Parking Code and/or abandoned vehicles and
trailers, and filing a civil complaint to recover towing and impounding charges
assessed to the City. (Ord. 2020-2, 8-13-2020)
CHAPTER 5
DYNAMIC BRAKING DEVICE
SECTION:
6-5-1: Definition
6-5-2: Use Prohibited
6-5-3: Penalty
6-5-1: DEFINITION:
"Dynamic braking device" is defined as a device used primarily on trucks for
the conversion of the engine from an internal combustion to air compressor for
the purpose of braking. Dynamic braking device is also commonly referred to as
a "Jacobs brake", "engine brake" or "compression brake". (Ord. 1998-3, 4-9-
1998)
6-5-2: USE PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate any motor vehicle with a dynamic
braking device engaged within the city. (Ord. 1998-3, 4-9-1998; amd. 2007 Code)
6-5-3: PENALTY:
Any person who violates this chapter shall, upon conviction, be subject to
penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 1998-3, 4-9-1998; amd. 2007 Code)
CHAPTER 6
JUNKED, ABANDONED VEHICLES 1
SECTION:
6-6-1: Definitions
6-6-2: Prohibited; Nuisance Declared
6-6-3: Responsibility
6-6-4: Notice; Hearing
6-6-5: Removal, Impoundment By City
6-6-6: Disposition Of Unclaimed Vehicles
6-6-7: Redemption
6-6-8: Special Permit; Fee
6-6-9: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 49-1801 et seq.
6-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, words and their
derivations shall have the meanings ascribed herein. When not inconsistent with
the context, words used in the present tense shall include the future, plural
words shall include the singular, and singular words shall include the plural.
The word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely directory.
DIRECTOR OF TRAFFIC: The chief of police or other city employee designated by
the mayor to serve in this capacity.
SUBJECT VEHICLE: Any "vehicle" as defined herein which does not have lawfully
affixed thereto both an unexpired license plate or plates and a current vehicle
safety inspection certificate, if the same are required by law, or which is
structurally damaged, dismantled, partially dismantled, junked, abandoned or
discarded.
VEHICLE: Any vehicle which is self-propelled and/or designed to travel along
the ground, on water or through the air, including, but not limited to,
aircraft, watercraft, automobiles, buses, motor bikes, motorcycles, motor
scooters, trucks, motor homes, tractors, go-carts, and golf carts, as well as
parts or appurtenances thereto; and it shall also include campers and trailers
which are neither inhabited nor affixed to a foundation. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-10-
1977)
6-6-2: PROHIBITED; NUISANCE DECLARED:
   A.   Prohibited: No person shall park, store, leave, abandon, or permit the
parking, storing, leaving or abandoning of any "subject vehicle" as defined
above, whether attended to or not, upon any public or private property within
the city for a period of time exceeding twenty four (24) hours.
   B.   Declared Nuisance: The presence of an inoperative vehicle, or parts
thereof, on private or public property is hereby declared to be a nuisance in
that it represents a serious hazard to the public health, safety, convenience
and welfare of the residents of the city. Such nuisance may be abated as
provided below. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-10-1977)
   C.   Exceptions: However, this chapter shall not apply to any vehicle
completely enclosed within a building on private property or any vehicle held
in connection with a business enterprise lawfully licensed by the city and
located in an area where such a business is permitted by the zoning laws of the
city. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-10-1977; amd. 2007 Code)
6-6-3: RESPONSIBILITY:
Upon proper notice and opportunity to be heard as specified below, the owner of
a subject vehicle and the owner or occupant of the private property on which
such vehicle is located, either or all of them, shall be responsible for its
prompt removal. In the event of removal and disposition by the city, the owner
of the vehicle and/or the owner or occupant of the private property where the
vehicle is located, shall be liable for the expenses incurred; provided, that
such liability shall not attach to the owner or occupant of the property if it
satisfactorily appears to the director of traffic that the vehicle in question
was placed on said property without the owner's or occupant's prior knowledge,
permission, or subsequent acquiescence. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-10-1977)
6-6-4: NOTICE; HEARING:
   A.   Notice To Abate: Whenever it comes to the attention of the director of
traffic that any "nuisance" as defined in section
6-6-2 of this chapter exists within the city, a notice, in writing, shall be
served upon the owner of the vehicle and the occupant of the property where the
nuisance exists, or in case there is no such occupant, then upon the owner of
the property or his agent, notifying them of the existence of the nuisance and
requesting its removal within fifteen (15) days following issuance of the
notice. The notice shall further advise that upon failure to comply with its
terms, the city or its designee shall undertake such removal with the costs
incurred thereby to be levied against the owner of the vehicle and/or the owner
or occupant of the property. If the owner of the vehicle and the owner or
occupant of the property cannot be located personally, it shall constitute
sufficient notice if a copy of the same is posted in a conspicuous place upon
the property and duplicate copies of the notice are sent by certified mail to
the owner of the vehicle and the owner or occupant of the property, if known,
at their last known addresses.
   B.   Request For Hearing: Persons to whom notices are directed or their duly
authorized agents, may file a written request for hearing before the city
council within the fifteen (15) day period prescribed herein, for the purpose
of showing cause why they should not be required to comply with the terms of
this chapter.
   C.   Hearing:
      1.   Notice: Such hearing shall be held at the next regularly scheduled
meeting of the city council at least five (5) days after the filing of the
request for hearing, and the persons to whom notices are directed shall be
advised by ordinary mail or personal delivery of the time and place of said
hearing at least five (5) days in advance thereof.
      2.   Time For Compliance Tolled: The time remaining for compliance with
the notice shall be tolled upon the filing of a request for hearing and shall
not again commence to run until the hearing has been conducted and the city
council has issued its decision.
      3.   Testimony; Evidence: At any such hearing, the city and the persons
to whom notices have been directed may introduce such witnesses and evidence as
either party deems necessary.
      4.   Council Decision: The city council shall decide whether or not the
vehicle in question should be impounded (unless impoundment has already
occurred as authorized below) and subject to disposition pursuant to this
chapter.
   D.   Hazard Exists:
      1.   Notice To Remove: Notwithstanding the forgoing provisions of this
section, if the director of traffic reasonably determines that the condition
and location of a subject vehicle represents a clear, present and serious
hazard to life, safety or health, he shall, without delay, attempt to ascertain
the identity of its owner and of the owner or occupant of property on which it
is found, and shall personally serve upon such person a written demand that the
vehicle be removed within twenty four (24) hours.
      2.   Removal By City: If the identity of such person cannot be readily
ascertained, or if there is a failure to comply with the demand for removal,
the director of traffic may remove and impound the vehicle as provided below,
and shall give notice of such action in the manner prescribed in section
6-6-5 of this chapter. Opportunity for hearing shall be granted as provided
above, except: a) a hearing may be requested after either notice to remove or
notice of impoundment, and that b) the person receiving notice may request, and
shall receive upon request, an accelerated hearing before a quorum of the city
council at a special meeting conducted no later than seven (7) days after
filing the request for such hearing. Notice of such hearing shall be personally
delivered or sent by ordinary mail no less than five (5) days in advance
thereof. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-10-1977)
6-6-5: REMOVAL, IMPOUNDMENT BY CITY:
   A.   Failure To Comply; Removal By City: If the violation described in the
notice has not been remedied within the compliance period, or if a hearing has
been conducted and the compliance period has expired following affirmance of
the violation by the city council, the director of traffic or his designee is
authorized to take possession of the vehicle in question and remove it from the
premises where it is located.
   B.   Interference Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person to
interfere with, hinder or deny access to the director of traffic or his
designee attempting to remove a vehicle as authorized by this chapter.
   C.   Notice Of Impoundment: Within forty eight (48) hours of the removal of
such vehicle, the director of traffic shall give notice to the owner of the
vehicle, to any known lienholder, and also to the owner or occupant of the
property from which the vehicle was removed, if known, that said vehicle has
been impounded and stored for violation of this chapter. The notice shall
specify the location where the vehicle is stored, and state the costs incurred
by the city for its removal and storage. Notice shall be delivered personally
or sent by ordinary mail. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-10-1977)
6-6-6: DISPOSITION OF UNCLAIMED VEHICLES:
   A.   Appraisal: If sixty (60) days elapse after removing a vehicle and
giving notice as authorized above, during which the vehicle has not been
claimed and the city's costs paid, the city shall cause the vehicle to be
appraised.
   B.   Value Less Than Costs Incurred By City: If the vehicle is appraised at
less than the costs incurred (including the advertising costs that would be
incurred if the vehicle were sold at public auction), the director of traffic
may then summarily dispose of the vehicle and execute an appropriate
certificate of sale or destruction. One copy of such certificate shall be filed
with the city clerk-treasurer and another shall be forwarded to the appropriate
office of the Idaho transportation department.
   C.   Value In Excess Of Costs:
      1.   Notice Of Sale: If the vehicle is appraised in excess of costs as
described above, the director of traffic shall post prominently in the city
municipal building and publish once in a newspaper of general circulation
within the city, a notice of public sale not less than ten (10) days before the
date of the proposed sale.
      2.   Contents Of Notice: Such notice of sale shall include:
         a.   A statement that the sale is of property impounded by the city;
         b.   A description of the vehicle sufficient to identify it; and
         c.   A recitation of the date, time, and place of sale.
      3.   Sale: The vehicle shall be sold for cash to the highest and best
bidder.
      4.   Certificate Of Sale: At the time of payment of the purchase price,
the director of traffic shall execute an appropriate certificate of sale, the
original to be given to the purchaser, one copy to be filed with the city
clerk-treasurer, and another copy to be forwarded to the appropriate office of
the Idaho transportation department.
      5.   Invalid Sale: Should the sale for any reason be invalid, the
liability of the city or its employees or agents shall be strictly limited to
the amount of the purchase price received.
      6.   Surplus Proceeds: Costs recovered in the course of any sale or
distribution shall be deposited to the appropriate law enforcement budget of
the city by the city clerk-treasurer and any surplus proceeds shall be paid to
the owner of the vehicle, or party holding a valid lien or security interest,
if known. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-10-1977)
6-6-7: REDEMPTION:
The owner of, or person asserting a lien or secured interest in, any vehicle
impounded under the provisions of this chapter may redeem such vehicle at any
time after its removal but prior to its sale or destruction upon proof of
ownership, lien or secured interest, and payment to the city clerk-treasurer of
such sum as the director of traffic shall determine and fix for the actual and
reasonable expense of removal and storage, plus any preliminary sale
advertising expenses already incurred. Usual removal, storage and advertising
expenses, reflecting the city's pattern of actual costs shall be posted in the
office of the director of traffic and shall be made available for public
inspection. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-10-1977)
6-6-8: SPECIAL PERMIT; FEE:
Upon application of any person for a special permit, accompanied by payment in
cash, certified check or money order of the sum of twenty five dollars
($25.00), the director of traffic shall cause a permit to be issued for salvage
of parts from one vehicle and/or for necessary repair of an existing vehicle.
Such permit shall be valid for a period not exceeding thirty (30) days. No more
than two (2) such permits may be obtained by any person or household during any
twelve (12) month period. When a permit has expired, if inspection by the
director of traffic or his designee discloses that the unused salvage has been
removed and/or the vehicle repaired by the permittee, the fee herein specified
shall be refunded; but if such salvage has not been removed and/or the vehicle
repaired within the specified time period, the director of traffic or his
designee shall issue a notice to remove as provided in section
6-6-4 of this chapter and shall proceed as directed by this chapter. The permit
fee shall be retained, crediting it against the city's cost. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-
10-1977)
6-6-9: PENALTY:
   A.   Civil Action: Upon failure of compliance with this chapter by the owner
of a vehicle or by the owner or occupant of property from which such vehicle
has been removed by the city, the city may file a civil action against any or
all of them to recover the unpaid expenses incurred by such removal, including
litigation costs and a reasonable attorney fee. In addition, as part of or
separately from the civil action, the city may cause a lien or special
assessment to be placed directly upon the property where the vehicle was
located for the amount of such expenses.
   B.   Misdemeanor: Any violation of a provision of this chapter shall be
unlawful and punishable as a misdemeanor. Each day that such violation
continues with respect to each vehicle may be deemed a separate offense.
Prosecution for such offense shall not preclude a civil action for recovery of
costs as provided above. (Ord. 1977-4, 8-10-1977)
CHAPTER 7
SNOWMOBILES 1
SECTION:
6-7-1: Definitions
6-7-2: Operation Within City Limits
6-7-3: Restrictions
6-7-4: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 67-7101 et seq.
6-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
HIGHWAY: All "highways" as defined by the law except for "public roadways" as
defined in this section.
OPERATOR: Each person who operates or is in physical control of the snowmobile.
OWNER: Any person holding any record title to a snowmobile and entitled to the
use or possession thereof, other than a lien holder or other person having a
security interest only.
PERSON: An individual, partnership, association, corporation, or any other body
or group of persons, whether incorporated or not, and regardless of the degree
of formal organization.
PUBLIC ROADWAY: Portions of all road or street, improved or designed, or
ordinarily used for travel or parking of motor vehicles, which is controlled by
an authority other than the state highway department.
SNOWMOBILE: Any self-propelled vehicle under one thousand (1,000) pounds'
unladen gross weight, designed primarily for travel on snow or ice, or over
natural terrain, which may be steered by tracks, skis, or runners, and which is
not otherwise registered or licensed under the laws of the state. (Ord. 1984-1,
1-18-1984)
6-7-2: OPERATION WITHIN CITY LIMITS:
Snowmobiles may not be operated within the city limits of the city from Main
Street from the west city limits to Third Avenue East except where necessary to
cross such streets to get from one side to the other. All other public streets
within the city shall be opened to travel on snowmobiles, subject to the
restrictions contained herein. (Ord. 1984-1, 1-18-1984)
6-7-3: RESTRICTIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person:
   A.   Speed: To drive or operate any snowmobile at any rate of speed greater
than that reasonable and prudent under the existing conditions.
   B.   Under Influence: To operate a snowmobile under the influence of
intoxicating liquor, narcotics, or habit forming drugs.
   C.   Negligent Manner: To operate a snowmobile in a negligent manner so as
to endanger the person or property of another, or to cause injury or damage to
either, or to harass, chase, or annoy any wild game animals or birds or
domestic animals.
   D.   Lights: To operate a snowmobile without a lighted headlight and
taillight between the hours of dusk and dawn and when upon crossing any public
roadway or highway, or when otherwise required for the safety of others.
   E.   Brakes: To operate a snowmobile without an adequate braking device
which may be operated by either hand or foot.
   F.   Muffler: To operate a snowmobile without an adequate muffler, except
when used in conjunction with public racing events.
   G.   Driver's License: To operate a snowmobile upon a public roadway or
highway without a valid motor vehicle operator's license, unless the public
roadway or highway is closed to other motor vehicle traffic.
   H.   Sidewalks: To operate or park snowmobiles on sidewalks.
   I.   Indiscriminate Operation: To operate a snowmobile indiscriminately
within the city limits of the city without a distinct point of departure and
point of destination. Such point of departure or destination can be either
within the city or outside the city.
   J.   Speed; Traffic Control: To disobey all posted speed limit and traffic
control signs.
   K.   Trailer Or Sled: To operate a snowmobile with a trailer or sled that
does not have a fixed hitch.
   L.   Right Of Way: To fail to yield the right of way to all motor vehicles
and pedestrians.
   M.   Hours Of Operation: To operate the snowmobile between the hours of ten
o'clock (10:00) P.M., and six o'clock (6:00) A.M., except when traveling to
residence by way of the designated snowmobile route.
   N.   Unlicensed, Unregistered Vehicle: To operate unlicensed, unregistered
snowmobiles. (Ord. 1984-1, 1-18-1984)
6-7-4: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any section of this chapter shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to penalty as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 1984-1, 1-18-1984; amd. 2007 Code)
CHAPTER 8
SKATEBOARDS, ROLLER SKATES OR BLADES, GO-CARTS 1
SECTION:
6-8-1: Purpose
6-8-2: Definitions
6-8-3: Use Restricted
6-8-4: Posted Property
6-8-5: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-313.
6-8-1: PURPOSE:
It is the intent of the city council to place reasonable limits on the
recreation of skateboarding, roller skates or blades, go-carts or scooters in
congested areas to protect the public and public or private improvements from
damage or liability occasioned as a result of the exercise of that recreational
activity. (Ord. 1992-4, 8-13-1992)
6-8-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the terms herein are defined as follows:
GO-CART: A small vehicle distinguished by small wheels capable of carrying one
or two (2) persons propelled by an engine and designed for use as a sport or
toy rather than transportation upon streets.
ROLLER SKATES OR BLADES: Skates with small wheels for use on a smooth surface.
SCOOTER: Small wheel carts or wagons upon or in which one or two (2) persons
may ride, having no engine, but is usually propelled by foot power, pushed by
another or allowed to coast downhill.
SKATEBOARD: Any short board composed of wood, plastic or other material to
which is attached roller skate type wheels upon which a person sits, stands,
kneels or lies while the device is in motion. (Ord. 1992-4, 8-13-1992)
6-8-3: USE RESTRICTED:
It is unlawful for any person to ride on or propel any skateboard, roller
skates or blades, go-carts or scooters on any of the following streets or
sidewalks adjacent to:
   A.   Main Street beginning at 4th West and Main to the Main Street river
bridge;
   B.   One block north and south of Main Street beginning at the intersection
of 4th West and Main to the intersection of 3rd East and Main.
   C.   Any other street or sidewalk with signs stating the prohibition. (Ord.
1992-4, 8-13-1992)
6-8-4: POSTED PROPERTY:
   A.   Prohibited: No person shall ride or propel any skateboard, roller
skates or blades, go-cart or scooter upon the land of another, public or
private, without the permission of the landowner or the tenant in possession
where such land has been posted by the landowner or tenant in possession in a
conspicuous manner upon or near the boundaries of such land with signs legibly
printed informing persons of said prohibition.
   B.   Right Of Entry: Law enforcement personnel are specifically authorized
to enter upon private property, when necessary, for the sole purpose of
enforcing this prohibition on a complaint signed by the landowner or tenant in
possession. (Ord. 1992-4, 8-13-1992)
6-8-5: PENALTY:
A violation of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor subject to penalty as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 1992-4, 8-13-1992; amd. 2007 Code)
TITLE 7
FIRE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
FIRE DISTRICT
SECTION:
7-1-1: District Established
7-1-1: DISTRICT ESTABLISHED:
The city is hereby declared to be and is hereby established as a fire district
and said fire district shall be known and designated as fire zones 1, 2, and 3.
Each zone shall include such territory or portions of the city as illustrated,
outlined, and designated on a certain map on file in the office of the city
clerk-treasurer being marked and designated as "Fire Zones Of The City Of Lava
Hot Springs" for the application of the regulations included in the
international building code, published by the International Code Council, and
any subsequent amendments, supplements, or editions of said document. (Ord.
1976-2, 4-23-1976; amd. Ord. 2003-3, 3-13-2003)
CHAPTER 2
FIREWORKS
SECTION:
7-2-1: Definitions
7-2-2: Permit Required
7-2-3: Sale Of Nonaerial Common Fireworks
7-2-4: Public Display
7-2-5: Requirements For Sale Of Nonaerial Common Fireworks
7-2-6: Requirements For Public Display Of Fireworks
7-2-7: Location
7-2-8: Prohibitions
7-2-9: Penalty
7-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
CITY: The City of Lava Hot Springs, Bannock County, Idaho.
FIREWORKS: Any combustible or explosive composition, or any substance or
combination of substances, or article prepared for the purpose of producing a
visible or audible effect by combustion, explosion, deflagration or detonation.
Fireworks include sky lanterns and similar devices and items classified as
common or special fireworks by the United States Bureau of Explosives or
contained in the regulations of the United States Department of Transportation
and designated as UN 0335 1.3G or UN 0336 1.4G. The term "fireworks" shall not
include any automotive safety flares, toy guns, toy cannons, caps or other
items designed for use with toy guns or toy cannons, party poppers, pop-its or
other devices which contain twenty five hundredths (0.25) of a grain or less of
explosive substance.
LANTERNS: Any Chinese lanterns, sky lanterns, wish lanterns, sky candles, fire
balloons or similar devices regardless of name using an open flame or
combustible material, including but not limited to alcohol or a candle, for the
purpose of illuminating, or heating the air in, a bag made of tissue paper,
rice paper, very thin plastic or any combustible material for the purpose of
making the device lighter than air causing it to rise into the sky or for the
purpose of floating the device on water. Because of the combustible nature of
these devices and the fire danger posed by such devices, these devices will be
considered fireworks and regulated as such by the City.
NON-AERIAL COMMON FIREWORKS: Means any fireworks such as ground spinners,
fountains, sparklers, smoke devices or snakes designed to remain on or near the
ground and not to travel outside a fifteen foot (15') diameter circle or emit
sparks or other burning material which land outside a twenty foot (20')
diameter circle or above a height of twenty feet (20'). Non-aerial common
fireworks do not include firecrackers, jumping jacks, lanterns, or similar
products.
PERMIT: An authorization given by the City for the sale of nonaerial fireworks
or for public display of fireworks or other events. (Ord. 2011-4, 12-8-2011;
amd. Ord. 2017-4, 10-5-2017)
7-2-2: PERMIT REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or use any fireworks at any time
not permitted by this chapter. (Ord. 2011-4, 12-8-2011)
7-2-3: SALE OF NONAERIAL COMMON FIREWORKS:
Nonaerial common fireworks may be sold at retail with a permit issued by the
City and used beginning at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight June 23, and ending
at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight July 5, and beginning at twelve o'clock (12:
00) midnight December 26 and ending at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight January
1. (Ord. 2011-4, 12-8-2011)
7-2-4: PUBLIC DISPLAY:
Fireworks for public display or other event may be used at any time in
compliance with a permit issued by the City. (Ord. 2011-4, 12-8-2011)
7-2-5: REQUIREMENTS FOR SALE OF NONAERIAL COMMON FIREWORKS:
Any person or entity desiring to engage in the retail sale of nonaerial common
fireworks shall:
   A.   Make application to the City on a form approved by the City.
   B.   Furnish to the City a certificate of public liability and property-
casualty insurance in the amount of one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00)
for personal injury and property damage.
   C.   Pay a fee to the City of twenty five dollars ($25.00) for the permit.
   D.   Display the permit in public view at the location listed in the permit.
(Ord. 2011-4, 12-8-2011)
7-2-6: REQUIREMENTS FOR PUBLIC DISPLAY OF FIREWORKS:
A person or entity desiring to engage in the public display of fireworks shall:
   A.   Make application to the City on a form approved by the City.
   B.   Furnish to the City a certificate of public liability and property-
casualty insurance providing coverage of one million dollars ($1,000,000.00)
for personal injury and property damage.
   C.   Pay a fee of one hundred twenty five dollars ($125.00) for the permit.
   D.   Ensure that the public display will be supervised by a qualified person
and will not constitute an unreasonable hazard to persons or property. (Ord.
2011-4, 12-8-2011)
7-2-7: LOCATION:
Retail sales of nonaerial common fireworks shall be allowed only from within a
temporary fireworks stand and shall be operated and comply with all provisions
of section 39-2607, Idaho Code. (Ord. 2011-4, 12-8-2011)
7-2-8: PROHIBITIONS:
The lighting, release and/or discharge of lanterns as defined in this chapter
is hereby prohibited within the corporate limits of the City of Lava Hot
Springs, Idaho. (Ord. 2017-4, 10-5-2017)
7-2-9: PENALTY:
   A.   Criminal Penalties: Any person or entity violating any provision of
this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor punishable by imprisonment in the
County Jail for a period not to exceed six (6) months, or by a fine not to
exceed one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), or by both such fine and imprisonment,
and shall be additionally responsible for restitution of all damages caused and
costs of fighting any fire caused by such violation.
   B.   Civil Penalties: Any person or entity violating any provision of this
chapter shall be responsible for the costs of suppressing any resulting fire,
including the wages paid by any responding agency and the reasonable charges
for equipment, materials and supplies used in the suppression of such resulting
fire. The City of Lava Hot Springs and/or any other agency responding to
suppress a fire caused by anyone violating any provision of this chapter shall
have the right to bring a civil lawsuit to recover such costs. (Ord. 2017-4,
10-5-2017)
CHAPTER 3
OPEN BURNING
SECTION:
7-3-1: Applicability
7-3-2: Definitions
7-3-3: Prohibited Materials
7-3-4: Incinerators, Burn Cages And Burn Barrels
7-3-5: Permissible Burning
7-3-6: Permit
7-3-7: Burning Moratorium
7-3-8: Responsibility And Duty Of Permit Holder Or Persons Responsible For
Fires
7-3-9: No Responsibility Of City
7-3-10: Recreational Fires
7-3-11: Penalty
7-3-1: APPLICABILITY:
This chapter shall apply to the burning of any materials within the City of
Lava Hot Springs, Bannock County, Idaho an incorporated City. (Ord. 2017-5, 2-
8-2018)
7-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
These definitions shall apply to this chapter.
BONFIRE: Means the open burning of cut trees, vegetation, leaves or lumber for
ceremonial, celebratory or other purposes, and wherein the fire occupies an
area greater than three feet (3') in diameter and two feet (2') in height.
BURN: Means all outdoor burning except a recreational fire or burning contained
in an incinerator burn barrel.
HAZARDOUS MATERIALS: Means those chemicals or substances whether the materials
are in usable or waste condition which are physical hazards or health hazards
as defined and classified in part V of the 2012 edition of the International
Fire Code or the part defining "hazardous materials" of the effective version
of such code as is adopted or approved by the Idaho Building Code Board or
Idaho Department of Insurance/State Fire Marshal, effective on January 1 of the
year following adoption by the Idaho Building Code Board or Idaho Department of
Insurance/State Fire Marshal.
OPEN BURNING: Means the burning of a bonfire, household garbage or rubbish fire
or other fire in an outdoor location where the fuel being burned is not
contained in an incinerator, burn barrel, outdoor fireplace or barbeque pit.
RECREATIONAL FIRE: Means the burning of materials other than household garbage
or rubbish where fuel being burned is not contained in a burn barrel,
incinerator, outdoor fireplace, fire ring, or pit and with a total fuel area of
three feet (3') or less in diameter and two feet (2') or less in height for
pleasure, religious, ceremonial, cooking or similar purposes. (Ord. 2017-5, 2-
8-2018)
7-3-3: PROHIBITED MATERIALS:
The burning of the following is prohibited, whether in an open burn or in an
incinerator, burn barrel, stove or fireplace:
   A.   Carcasses and parts of carcasses from dead animals including
domesticated livestock, sheep, goats, poultry, pets, and commercial fish and
animal feces;
   B.   Junked motor vehicles or any materials resulting from a salvage
operation;
   C.   Tires or other rubber materials or products;
   D.   Plastics;
   E.   Asphalt or composition roofing or any other asphaltic material or
products;
   F.   Tar, tar paper, waste or heavy petroleum products, or paints;
   G.   Lumber or timber treated with preservatives, including railroad ties;
   H.   Trade waste materials meaning any solid, liquid or gaseous material
resulting from the construction or demolition of any structure, or the
operation of any business, trade or industry including, but not limited to,
wood product industry waste such as saw dust, bark, peelings, chips, shavings
and cull wood except as specifically allowed under IDAPA 58.01.01 section 600 -
623;
   I.   Insulated wire;
   J.   Pathogenic waste;
   K.   Hazardous waste;
   L.   Any material which, when burned, will produce an offensive smell, smoke
or odor;
   M.   Any material which, when burned, will cause or create dense smoke or
odor; and
   N.   Garbage/household waste. (Ord. 2017-5, 2-8-2018)
7-3-4: INCINERATORS, BURN CAGES AND BURN BARRELS:
   A.   Use of incinerators, burn cages or burn barrels are prohibited within
the City of Lava Hot Springs as a routine method of trash disposal, except that
a burn cage, barrel or other forms of containment may be used when burning yard
waste pursuant to an issued burn permit.
   B.   All burning in the burn barrel, burn cage or incinerator shall be done
during daylight hours; any fire still burning at sunset shall be extinguished
by water, fire extinguishment materials or by other appropriate means.
   C.   Incinerators or burn barrels may only be used to burn organic yard
waste (limbs, leaves, etc.) grown on the property where used. In accordance
with the Clean Air Act and associated regulations, burn barrels or incinerators
may not be used to burn household garbage, prohibited items described in
section
7-3-3 of this chapter, or other products prohibited by State or Federal
regulations. (Ord. 2017-5, 2-8-2018)
7-3-5: PERMISSIBLE BURNING:
   A.   Except for recreational fires, burning of permissible materials may be
done outside of a burn barrel, burn cage or incinerator upon compliance with
all the following:
      1.   A permit to engage in such burning, except for a recreational fire,
burn barrel, burn cage or incinerator, shall be obtained from the City Clerk or
the City Clerk's designee at the City Clerk's Office.
      2.   All burning shall be constantly attended by a competent person over
the age of eighteen (18) until the fire is extinguished.
      3.   A minimum of one portable fire extinguisher with a minimum 4-
A rating or other approved on-site fire extinguishing equipment, such as dirt,
sand, water barrel, garden hose or water truck, shall be available for
immediate utilization.
      4.   The location for open burning shall not be less than fifty feet
(50') from any structure or combustible object including trees and shrubbery,
and provisions shall be made to prevent the fire from spreading within fifty
feet (50') of any structure or combustible object.
      5.   Such burning shall be done at a distance of more than two hundred
feet (200') from any wild land or sage brush area.
      6.   The person to whom the permit is issued shall have the legal right,
by ownership, lease or written permission, to conduct the burn at the time and
place proposed. It shall not be the responsibility of the City Clerk or any
other City employee or agent to verify the accuracy of their presentations and
information provided by the person seeking the permit and the person seeking
the permit shall be completely and fully responsible for any inaccuracies in
the information provided in support of issuance of the permit.
      7.   The permit holder shall be responsible for following safe practices
for the burn, including not starting or continuing the burn during unsafe
conditions which shall include, but are not limited to, dry conditions, low
humidity, strong winds or other conditions which could reasonably be expected
to make burning hazardous to persons or property. It is recommended that burns
not be conducted when the wind exceeds or is expected to exceed five (5) mph
during the anticipated duration of the fire. This is only a recommendation and
is not intended to alleviate the permit holder's obligation and responsibility
for following safe burn practices.
      8.   No burn shall create dense smoke, toxic emissions or odor. No burn
shall be conducted at a place or under conditions which are likely to or do
result in smoke, toxic emissions, odor or heat entering or damaging neighboring
structures. No burn shall be conducted in a place or under conditions which are
likely to or do result in a traffic hazard.
      9.   If hazardous conditions exist in the vicinity of the target area or
the burn, including but not limited to, dry or drought conditions causing the
vegetation or other fuels outside of the target area to be susceptible to
ignition, which could be reasonably expected to permit the burn to spread
beyond the target area, the permit holder shall be responsible for eliminating
the hazardous conditions by creating borders, perimeters and barriers to
prevent the burn from spreading beyond the target area.
      10.   No burn shall be conducted at night between dusk and dawn.
      11.   The permit holder shall in all instances notify the dispatcher for
the Bannock County Sheriff's Office of the location, expected start time and
expected duration of all burns for which a permit is required. (Ord. 2017-5, 2-
8-2018)
7-3-6: PERMIT:
   A.   A permit is required in all cases except for a recreational fire,
burning inside in a fireplace, wood stove or cook stove. The Lava Hot Springs
City Fire Chief, City Code Enforcement Officer, City Clerk or the City Clerk's
designee is authorized to issue a permit for burning. The purpose of the permit
is to provide a record of the authorized time and target area for the burn and
to identify the person responsible for conducting the burn. Obtaining a permit
shall not alleviate the permit holder from seeking and obtaining permits from
any other agency that has jurisdiction of the target area and/or materials to
be burned. All permits are subject to revocation or suspension after issuance
at the sole discretion of the Lava Hot Springs City Fire Chief and/or City Code
Enforcement Officer if determined that conditions warrant revocation or
suspension of the permit. The Lava Hot Springs City Fire Chief, City Code
Enforcement Officer, City Clerk or City Clerk's designee shall take reasonable
steps to notify the permit holder of such revocation or suspension, but it is
the responsibility of the permit holder to exercise due caution and diligence
for identifying hazardous conditions before starting a burn. The application
and permit shall be in a form authorized and furnished by the Lava Hot Springs
City Fire Chief, City Code Enforcement Officer and/or City Clerk. The
application and permit shall provide at least the following information:
      1.   The target area of the burn;
      2.   The expected start time and duration of the burn;
      3.   The materials to be burned;
      4.   The name, address and phone number of the person applying for the
permit who shall also be the person responsible for conducting the burn;
      5.   The beginning and end date during which the burn is authorized, but
in no case shall the authorized dates exceed two (2) weeks from the date of
issuance; and
      6.   Any special limits on or conditions applicable to the authorized
burn. (Ord. 2017-5, 2-8-2018)
7-3-7: BURNING MORATORIUM:
The Lava Hot Springs City Fire Chief and/or the Mayor or City Council may
declare a moratorium on burning, which moratorium shall revoke any permit
issued under this chapter for such period of time as in the sole discretion of
the Lava Hot Springs City Fire Chief and/or the Mayor or City Council is deemed
necessary to avoid increased fire hazards due to hazardous conditions. At the
discretion of the Lava Hot Springs Fire Chief and/or Mayor or City Council,
non-permitted recreational fires may be included in an issued burning
moratorium. Such moratorium when issued will be posted at Lava Hot Springs City
Hall and other sites where official public notices are customarily posted.
(Ord. 2017-5, 2-8-2018)
7-3-8: RESPONSIBILITY AND DUTY OF PERMIT HOLDER OR PERSONS RESPONSIBLE FOR
FIRES:
It is the responsibility of the applicant for a burn and the person supervising
any burn in a burn barrel, burn cage, incinerator or recreational fire to keep
the fire under control. If conditions exist immediately prior to beginning a
burn which violate section
7-3-4 or
7-3-5 of this chapter, the burn shall not be started. Even if such conditions
do not exist at the start of the burn the applicant for a burn and the person
supervising any burn in a burn barrel, burn cage, incinerator or recreational
fire shall have the duty to immediately bring the fire under control and/or
extinguish the fire to avoid accidental or unintended damage to property or
injury to persons. (Ord. 2017-5, 2-8-2018)
7-3-9: NO RESPONSIBILITY OF CITY:
The City of Lava Hot Springs and the issuing person shall have no liability for
any damage caused by any fire started by a permit holder or any fire which a
permit holder fails to extinguish when necessary to prevent accidental or
unintended damage to property or injury to persons.
The City of Lava Hot Springs and the issuing person shall have no liability for
failing to personally communicate the revocation or suspension of a permit
issued under this chapter to the permit holder. (Ord. 2017-5, 2-8-2018)
7-3-10: RECREATIONAL FIRES:
Small recreational fires as described in section
7-3-2 of this chapter may be conducted without a burn permit provided such
recreational fire is conducted in a safe manner and in keeping with the
provisions of this chapter. Any recreational fire exceeding the size
restrictions described in subsection A1 of this section, will constitute a
"bonfire" and may not be conducted without a permit.
   A.   The following rules and conditions shall apply to all recreational
fires:
      1.   Location: Recreational fires must be contained in an appropriate pit
below grade, or containment ring or structure of non-combustible material such
as metal or stone, and covered with a grate or screen not to exceed one-half
inch (1/2") mesh. Such pit, ring or containment must be located at least twenty
five feet (25') from a structure or combustible material including trees and
shrubbery, and be at least fifteen feet (15') from any portable or mobile
property such as vehicles, recreational vehicles, tents, or movable structures.
Recreational fires shall not exceed three feet (3') in diameter and two feet
(2') in height.
      2.   Precautions: All adult persons present at a recreational fire shall
be responsible to make sure that fire extinguishing equipment, including but
not limited to water buckets, shovels or garden hoses are readily available and
capable of use to extinguish a recreational fire or its spread.
      3.   Attendance: A competent person over the age of eighteen (18) shall
be present at all times at a recreational fire from its start to its
extinguishment.
      4.   Recreational Fire Bans: Although recreational fires are allowed
without a permit, the Mayor and City Council and/or the Lava Hot Springs City
Fire Chief may declare a temporary ban on recreational fires if in their sole
discretion such ban is deemed to be necessary to avoid increased fire hazards
due to adverse conditions, environmental or other factors. It is the
responsibility of the person or persons conducting such a fire to determine if
a moratorium is in place that affects recreational fires.
      5.   Materials: Prohibited materials as identified in section
7-3-3 of this chapter shall not be burned in a recreational fire. (Ord. 2017-5,
2-8-2018)
7-3-11: PENALTY:
   A.   Criminal Penalties: Any person or entity violating any provision of
this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor punishable by imprisonment in the
County Jail for a period not to exceed six (6) months, or by a fine not to
exceed one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), or by both such fine and imprisonment,
and shall be additionally responsible for restitution of all damages caused and
costs of fighting any fire caused by such violation.
   B.   Civil Penalties: Any person or entity violating any provision of this
chapter shall be responsible for the costs of suppressing any resulting fire,
including the wages paid by any responding agency and the reasonable charges
for equipment, materials and supplies used in the suppression of such resulting
fire. The City of Lava Hot Springs and/or any other agency responding to
suppress a fire caused by anyone violating any provision of this chapter shall
have the right to bring a civil lawsuit to recover such costs. (Ord. 2017-5, 2-
8-2018)
TITLE 8
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
SIDEWALKS 1
SECTION:
8-1-1: Snow And Ice
8-1-2: Construction, Repair Or Replacement
8-1-3: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-313.
8-1-1: SNOW AND ICE:
   A.   Removal Required: The owner, tenant or occupant of any premises within
the City abutting or adjoining any public sidewalk shall remove all snow and
ice from any such sidewalk daily.
   B.   Notice: The City Clerk-Treasurer or other duly authorized
representative is hereby authorized and empowered to notify, in writing, the
owner, tenant or occupant to comply with the terms and conditions of this
chapter to remove or otherwise correct the objectionable matter herein
legislated against, which notice notifying such owner, tenant or occupant that
they have a period of twelve (12) hours from and after receipt of such notice
or posting of such notice in a conspicuous place on the premises, within which
to correct or otherwise remove snow and ice. (Ord. 2017-1, 8-10-2017)
8-1-2: CONSTRUCTION, REPAIR OR REPLACEMENT:
   A.   Notice: At any time the City Council finds there is a safety hazard to
normal pedestrian traffic upon any sidewalk or where there is not a sidewalk
for pedestrian traffic, on streets designated for sidewalks by resolution of
the City Council, it shall be the duty of the City, or its authorized
representative, to notify the owners of premises within the City abutting or
adjoining any public street or sidewalk to construct a new sidewalk, or to
replace or repair such sidewalk, as necessary.
   B.   Cost: The owner of the abutting or adjoining property to said sidewalk
shall have the duty to construct, repair, or replace said sidewalk, at his own
cost and expense, upon receiving notification from the City. If the property
owner fails to construct, repair, or replace said sidewalk, within the time
period allotted to said owner, the City may cause the same to be constructed,
repaired or replaced and assess the cost thereof to the property owner in
accordance with section 50-1008, Idaho Code.
   C.   Time Limitations: The owner shall, after notice has been given: 1)
repair such sidewalk, within thirty (30) days; 2) replace such sidewalk, within
sixty (60) days; or 3) construct a new sidewalk, within sixty (60) days in
accordance with specifications set forth by the City Council in such notice, or
as may be set forth in the current edition, as amended, of the Idaho Standards
for Public Works Construction, if adopted by the City Council. Prior to said
construction, the owner shall advise the City of the date and time of said
construction, and shall further coordinate with the City for the construction
of adjoining curb and/or gutter. The City shall be responsible for the cost of
the construction of the curb and gutter. However, the City Council shall have
the discretion to construct curb and gutter, and/or to determine if curb and
gutter are needed, and if determined to not be needed, the City shall have no
responsibility to construct the same. (Ord. 2015-8, 11-12-2015)
8-1-3: PENALTY:
   A.   Failure To Comply: Upon failure of owner, tenant or occupant of said
premises to comply with the terms and conditions of such notice, then and in
that event such person shall be in violation of this chapter and subject to
action to be taken by the City.
   B.   Abatement By City: Upon the failure to remove snow and ice within the
time limits of section
8-1-1 of this chapter, the City may remove the same, doing whatever is
necessary to accomplish the abatement cleanup, removal and related work. The
costs thereof may be assessed against the property and collected as provided by
law, particularly as provided by Idaho Code title 50, chapter 10, for special
assessments, or the City may collect the costs by civil action. (Ord. 2017-1,
8-10-2017)
CHAPTER 2
TREES, SHRUBS, HEDGES AND OTHER PLANTS
SECTION:

8-2-2: Purpose
8-2-3: Definitions

8-2-5: Term Of Office
