10-3-10: Requirements For Contractor
10-3-11: Hotels And Restaurants
10-3-12: Street Litter Cans
10-3-13: Burning Prohibited 1  (Rep. by Ord. 2017-5, 2-8-2018)
10-3-14: Dumping Prohibited
10-3-15: Suppression Of Nuisances
10-3-16: Interference
10-3-17: Emergency Complaints
10-3-18: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. See title 7, chapter 3 of this Code.
10-3-1: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the MUNICIPAL REFUSE COLLECTION
SERVICE ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF LAVA HOT SPRINGS, IDAHO. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-
1972)
10-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter the following terms, phrases, words, and their
derivations shall have the meaning given herein. When not inconsistent with the
context words in the present tense include the future, words in the plural
number include the singular number, and words in the singular number include
the plural number. The word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely
directory.
ASHES: The residue from burning of wood, coal, coke or other combustible
material.
CITY: The City of Lava Hot Springs.
COLLECTOR: The City of Lava Hot Springs or the person holding a contract issued
or granted by the City authorizing such person to operate, conduct and maintain
a Municipal garbage and refuse collection and disposal system upon, on and over
streets, alleys and public ways of City.
GARBAGE: Putrescible animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the handling,
preparation, cooking and consumption of food.
OWNER AND OCCUPANT: Every "person" as herein defined in possession, charge,
custody or control of any premises where garbage, refuse and rubbish is created
or accumulated.
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind.
PREMISES: Land and all dwellings and structures thereon including, but not
excluding, by enumeration, single- or multi-family dwellings, rooming houses,
apartment houses, hospitals, convalescent and nursing homes, hotels, and
motels, restaurants, drive-in establishments or place of conducting business,
trade or occupation.
REFUSE: All putrescible and nonputrescible solid waste (except body waste)
including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street cleanings, small dead animals and
solid market and industrial wastes.
RUBBISH: Nonputrescible solid waste (excluding ashes) consisting of both
combustible and noncombustible waste, such as paper, cardboard, tin cans, yard
clippings, wood, glass, bedding, crockery, and similar materials.
SANITARY CONTAINERS: Approved sanitary containers or receptacles of not less
than twenty (20) gallon capacity, not more than thirty two (32) gallon capacity
or as provided in subsection
10-3-9A of this chapter and may be any of the following:
   A.   Disposable (nonreturnable) paper sacks, which shall be fifty (50) pound
wet strength extensible kraft paper.
   B.   Disposable (nonreturnable) plastic bags, which shall be manufactured
from polyethylene copolymer resin, with the gauge of not less than 1.5 mils.
   C.   Metal or plastic cans which must not have any inside structures to
prevent the free discharge of the contents.
   D.   The aforesaid paper sacks or plastic bags may be used as liners in
cans, but such sacks or bags used as liners shall be watertight, of a solid and
durable material and shall be equipped with a suitable close fitting cover.
   E.   Approved mechanical dumping containers of one yard or more capacity.
TRASH: Nonputrescible solid waste such as excelsior, rags, wooden boxes or
cardboard or paper boxes, bottles, broken ware, small metal scraps, small
mechanical parts, shavings, floor sweepings excluding dirt floors, and all
other things of similar nature. The term "trash" as used in this chapter shall
not include debris resulting from construction, reconstruction or repairs of
premises, automobile frames, fallen trees, large tree limbs, nor other waste
matter that is not properly contained as specified in this chapter. (Ord. 1972-
1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-3: GARBAGE COLLECTION:
The city refuse collection and disposal service shall, by such means as the
city council deems appropriate, collect and dispose of all garbage, rubbish,
refuse, paper, glass, tin cans, crockery, ashes and other debris and shall
operate this service, and the regulations provided by this chapter shall be and
remain applicable thereto until duly amended as provided by law. The right and
power to amend this chapter from time to time and to repeal the same is
reserved to the city. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-4: SEPARATION OF REFUSE:
All kitchen garbage shall be drained of excess water and shall be wrapped in
paper. Any animal defecation shall be separately wrapped in paper before being
placed in said garbage can. Tin cans and glass containers shall be placed in
cans with kitchen garbage. Other rubbish, refuse, ashes, or other debris shall
be placed in containers separate from kitchen garbage. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-5: COLLECTION:
   A.   Collection Required: All garbage, refuse, rubbish, and ashes from the
entire residential sections properly placed for collection as provided for in
this chapter, shall be collected by the city or its duly authorized agent or
contractor necessary to maintain and preserve sanitation of the community.
   B.   Failure To Collect: Temporary failure to make such collection due to
circumstances beyond the control of the city shall not relieve the occupant or
the owner of the premises from the payment of sanitary service fees hereinafter
provided for.
   C.   Permit Required: No person, whether having entered into a contract with
the city for collections of garbage, refuse, rubbish and ashes or not, shall be
permitted to transport same over the public thoroughfares in anything other
than watertight containers and not until they shall have first secured a
written permit authorizing such hauling from the sanitary inspector.
   D.   Vehicles: The city or city's contractor shall furnish vehicles
especially designed for the collection and hauling of garbage and waste
products. All garbage vehicles shall be closed and watertight with side, rear
or both side and rear openings, commonly known as packers, for collecting
material. Rear loading openings shall have a minimum size of forty eight inches
by sixty inches (48" x 60"). (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-6: USE OF SERVICE COMPULSORY; EXCEPTION:
No person shall be permitted to refuse to accept the refuse collection and
disposal service herein provided for, and the failure of any person to receive
such service shall not exempt such person from the payment of charges herein
provided, save and except any of those persons residing in areas where no
service is rendered by the city, no charge will be made. The boundaries within
the city exempted from such charges shall be established by the city council.
(Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972; amd. 2007 Code)
10-3-7: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The city council is hereby empowered to prepare and publish rules and
regulations in connection with the preparation, handling and disposal of
garbage and refuse, subject to the approval of the city council, and may direct
that the city garbage and waste disposal crew or authorized contractor shall
not collect garbage and other waste from any premises where such rules and
regulations are not complied with. The failure to collect the same by such
direction shall not relieve the owner or occupant of such premises from the
payment of fees or penalties provided for herein. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972; amd.
2007 Code)
10-3-8: REGULATION OF GARBAGE AND REFUSE HAULING:
   A.   Watertight Containers Required: No person shall be permitted to collect
or haul garbage, refuse, ashes, or rubbish over the streets excepting that such
shall be conveyed in watertight containers.
   B.   Canvass Or Other Top Required: No person shall be permitted to collect
or haul garbage, refuse, rubbish, debris, papers or any other such items over
and across the streets and alleys thereof unless such vehicle so conveying such
rubbish or debris is equipped with a canvas top or some other device effective
to prevent the said rubbish, debris and trash from being strewn and littered
about the streets and alleys.
   C.   Hauling For Hire:
      1.   License Required: No person shall convey rubbish or garbage over and
across the streets and alleys for hire or for any person other than himself
unless he shall have first filed with the clerk-treasurer an application for
permission to haul garbage or rubbish over and across the streets and alleys
and until said application has been accepted and a license duly issued.
      2.   Form Of Application: That the application so made to the clerk-
treasurer for the person from whom such application is required shall be in
essentially the following form:
Licenses truck has license number                
Capacity of applicant's truck is                 tons volume of body of truck.
Persons with whom applicant has contract to haul garbage or rubbish at date of
making this application are:
   1.
                                                                           
   2.
                                                                           
   3.
                                                                          
                                                 
            Applicant's signature
   (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972)
      3.   Insurance: Before any license herein provided for can be issued by
the clerk-treasurer for the performance of hauling such garbage or rubbish,
such applicant shall file with the clerk-treasurer proof of workers'
compensation insurance and liability insurance. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972; amd.
2007 Code)
      4.   Hauling For Others Restricted: It shall be unlawful for any person
to haul garbage or rubbish for hire, or for any person other than himself, or
to permit hauling of any garbage or rubbish over the streets whatsoever, unless
he shall have made application for and received a license herein provided.
      5.   Use Of Approved Landfill Site Required: Any person who shall haul
garbage or rubbish in and about the city and haul the same over the streets
shall be required to haul all such rubbish and garbage to an approved landfill
site. This requirement, however, may be waived by special application and
permission granted by the city council.
      6.   Strewing Or Scattering Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any
person herein to permit general construction material, debris, tree limbs and
such refuse and garbage to be strewn or scattered about the streets. It shall
be unlawful for any person to carry garbage or rubbish about the streets unless
said refuse or garbage shall be properly covered so as to prevent the same from
being strewn about the streets or alleys. The violation of any of the
provisions of this section shall not only constitute a violation of this
chapter, but in those cases in which a license has been issued shall subject
such licensee to the cancellation of his license during the period for which it
was issued.
      7.   Power Of City Council: The city council is empowered to accept or
reject any application that may be made to haul garbage or refuse as provided
in this chapter.
      8.   Term Of License: Licenses herein required will be issued with
expiration date of December 30 of each year, unless said license shall be
cancelled by the council as provided for herein. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-9: GARBAGE, TRASH AND OTHER REFUSE FROM PRIVATE PROPERTY:
   A.   Containers: Oil drums, waste tubs, and similar containers shall not be
used for garbage and ashes. Worn out or unsightly garbage cans are to be
discarded.
   B.   Preparation Of Refuse:
      1.   Ashes: All ashes when placed for collection shall be cold and free
from any fire, live coals, or other substances which might ignite. Metal
containers with suitable handles or bails may be used for ashes only, if not
more than fifteen inches (15") in diameter or twenty four inches (24") high and
weigh, when full, less than seventy five (75) pounds.
      2.   Tree Limbs: Small tree limbs when tied in one man bundles not over
four feet (4') long will be hauled.
      3.   Magazines And Papers: Magazines and papers shall be tied in bundles
and must not be put out in wet weather earlier than twelve (12) hours before
pick up time.
      4.   Grass Cuttings, Weeds: Baskets or small cartons may be used for
grass cuttings, weeds, leaves, hedge trimmings and lawn raking. All items in
this subsection will be hauled away on schedule by the garbage contractor.
   C.   Containers, Placement For Collection: All garbage, refuse and rubbish,
except ashes, in or about any private residence, dwelling house or other
building shall be placed in sanitary containers and shall be placed at or near
the alley line if there is a public alley, right of way, or if there is no
access to the alley from the dwelling or other building, then such receptacle
shall be placed at or near the street line so as to be easily seen. The city
council will designate the pick up point for each residence, dwelling house or
other building. Refuse generating property not abutting public streets or
alleys shall permit access to the city or its refuse collection agency for the
collection and disposal of refuse placed thereon in approved sanitary
containers.
   D.   Missed Pick Up: If the collector should miss a refuse pick up and the
city or the collector is so notified prior to two o'clock (2:00) P.M. on such
day, such refuse will be removed the same day.
   E.   Removal Of Containers After Pick Up; Shelter Required: Removal of
garbage cans from the streets and alleys shall be made within twelve (12) hours
after pick up; provided, that such cans shall not be placed under the eaves of
any garage or any other building except in cases of absolute necessity; and in
case of such necessity, a roof or shelter shall be placed over such garbage
can.
   F.   Materials Not Picked Up: Books, broken concrete, rocks, plaster,
discarded building materials, or trees and large tree limbs are not included as
garbage. Oil drums and incinerators will not be emptied, nor will they be
allowed in alleys.
   G.   Owner Responsibility: Each property owner or tenant in the city shall
be held responsible for the cleanliness of one-half (1/2) of the alley adjacent
to his property. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-10: REQUIREMENTS FOR CONTRACTOR:
   A.   Districts; Collection Routes: The entire area within the city limits
shall be divided into districts for collection routes, and each district or
collection route shall be served the same day in each week or as needed for
industrial and commercial refuse removal except when a recognized holiday is
observed by the City or contractor or when a severe storm makes it impossible
to cover the route in the usual time. When the schedule has been disrupted for
any reason, the public will be so notified and service will be restored as soon
as possible and the public advised, if practical.
   B.   Equipment; Employees/Workers: The contractors shall furnish approved
equipment and men to cover the entire City each week.
   C.   Emptying Of Containers: After dumping the cans, employees shall return
them to the location from which they were taken and shall replace the covers.
Space about the cans and truck shall be left free from any refuse spilled
during the collection. This shall not be interpreted to mean that the collector
is responsible for cleaning up conditions about refuse cans caused by
carelessness of the tenant. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-11: HOTELS AND RESTAURANTS:
   A.   Receptacles Required: Every owner or lessee or person in charge of any
store, restaurant, cafe, hotel or other similar place where garbage is made or
accumulated shall provide or cause to be provided for such store, restaurant,
cafe or hotel or other similar building a watertight metal receptacle into
which all garbage shall be placed, and said receptacle shall have a
tightfitting cover and shall be kept covered. The dimensions of receptacle
shall be similar in size and weight as designated for residences.
   B.   Wastepaper: Loose papers, wastebasket material, wastepaper excelsior,
etc., must be placed in a container with a watertight lid. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-
1972)
10-3-12: STREET LITTER CANS:
Litter and waste disposal containers are not to be used by the merchants and
store employees for store and sidewalk sweeping, trash, paper or cartons. They
are for pedestrians to use to deposit gum wrappers, empty sacks or other
wrappers, preventing the littering upon the City sidewalks and street gutters.
Debris resulting from the construction or repairs of premises shall not be
placed with other refuse for collection but shall be disposed of directly by
the person owning, occupying or leasing the premises. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-13: BURNING PROHIBITED 1 :
(Rep. by Ord. 2017-5, 2-8-2018)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 7, chapter 3 of this Code.
10-3-14: DUMPING PROHIBITED:
   A.   Vacant Lots: It shall be unlawful for any person to incinerate garbage,
refuse, rubbish or ashes or dump same on vacant lots.
   B.   Dropping Or Spilling: No person including the contract agent authorized
to collect garbage, refuse, rubbish, and ashes shall drop, spill or permit same
to fall upon any private grounds or public street, alley or way. (Ord. 1972-1,
8-10-1972)
10-3-15: SUPPRESSION OF NUISANCES:
The Department of Sanitation shall take cognizance of all nuisances within the
limits of their sanitary jurisdiction and take such measures as may be
effectual to suppress and abate the same. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-16: INTERFERENCE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere with or obstruct the City
Council during the performance of their duties under this chapter. (Ord. 1972-
1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-17: EMERGENCY COMPLAINTS:
Provisions shall be made by the contractor or City Council to take care of
emergency complaints when refuse has not been collected upon the regular
scheduled trip and to take care of all other special or emergency calls. (Ord.
1972-1, 8-10-1972)
10-3-18: PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to
penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 1972-1, 8-10-1972; amd. 2007 Code)
CHAPTER 4
WATER, SEWER AND GARBAGE RATES
SECTION:
10-4-1: Purpose
10-4-2: Water Charges
10-4-3: Refuse Collection And Sanitation Rates
10-4-4: Domestic And Commercial Sewer Rates
10-4-5: Billing; Payment
10-4-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to establish domestic and commercial rates for
the use of the public sewer system for users inside and outside the corporate
limits of the city, and to revise and consolidate in this chapter the rates to
be assessed for metered water and for city refuse collection and sanitation
services, inside and outside the city. (Ord. 1993-1, 4-8-1993, eff. 4-15-1993)
10-4-2: WATER CHARGES:
Water charges shall be set by city council resolution. (Ord. 2004-3, 9-23-2004)
10-4-3: REFUSE COLLECTION AND SANITATION RATES:
There shall be a monthly fee to all commercial and/or residential users of
municipal refuse collection and other sanitation services assessed according to
contractor rates, plus an additional forty cent ($0.40) city administrative fee
per container. Each residential household user will be assessed an additional
three dollars sixty cents ($3.60) per month for landfill construction and
maintenance fees. The fees, rates, and charges for all commercial and/or
residential users of the city refuse collection system, and for landfill
construction and maintenance, may be changed from time to time hereafter by
resolution of the city council. (Ord. 2006-4, 11-16-2006)
10-4-4: DOMESTIC AND COMMERCIAL SEWER RATES:
   A.   Within City Limits: There shall be a monthly fee assessed to users of
the public sewer system which shall be calculated as follows: (Ord. 1993-1, 4-
8-1993, eff. 4-15-1993)
      1.   The monthly fee for each user shall be the user's sewer charge
multiplied by the constant monthly cost factor as established in section
10-2-8 of this title. (Ord. 1993-1, 4-8-1993, eff. 4-15-1993; amd. Ord. 2007-6,
10-11-2007)
      2.   Each user's service charge shall be determined in accordance with
chapter 2 of this title.
      3.   The constant monthly cost factor established herein shall be at the
discretion of the mayor and city council and updated from time to time to
reflect the actual costs of operation, maintenance, replacement and financing
of the sewage collection facility. (Ord. 1993-1, 4-8-1993, eff. 4-15-1993)
   B.   Outside City Limits: The sewer user charge for the use of the sewer
system outside of the city limits shall be computed by multiplying the number
of equivalent users determined from the schedules set out in chapter 2 of this
title. (Ord. 1995-2, 4-13-1995)
10-4-5: BILLING; PAYMENT:
   A.   Monthly Billing: Fees assessed for metered water, refuse collection and
sanitation services and sewage collection and treatment shall be billed to
users on a monthly basis unless otherwise determined and approved by the mayor
and city council. Domestic and/or commercial premises occupied for a period of
less than one month shall be assessed and billed for the entire month.
   B.   Combined Billing: Fees assessed for metered water, refuse collection
and sanitation services and sewage collection and treatment shall be combined
in one monthly bill and mailed or otherwise delivered to users monthly in the
month following that month for which services were rendered.
   C.   Due Date: The fee assessed for services shall become due and payable
fifteen (15) days from the date of mailing, or other delivery of each monthly
billing. When the fifteenth day falls upon a legal holiday or on a day when the
city offices are not open for business, the next regular business day shall be
considered the final due date. Where remittances are made by mail, assessed
fees shall be deemed paid on the date of mailing as shown by the postmark.
   D.   Delinquent Charge; Interest: A delinquent charge of ten percent (10%)
shall be added to each delinquent bill for each period of thirty (30) days'
delinquency or fraction thereof. Interest at the rate of one and one-half
percent (11/2%) per month or eighteen percent (18%) per annum shall be charged
on the accrued balance of any delinquent account.
   E.   Discontinuance Of Service: When assessed fees are not paid within
thirty (30) days after the due date, the city may collect such billing in any
lawful manner and may issue an order to discontinue any or all such services to
a delinquent customer.
   F.   Notice To Owner: In the event that the user is not the owner in
possession, should the account become delinquent for sixty (60) days, the owner
of said premises shall be notified, in writing, by the city of the account and
its delinquency.
   G.   Responsibility For Payment: The owner of such premises is primarily
liable for any charges delineated in this chapter. Partial payment of any
tenant shall not constitute a waiver by the city of any amounts due hereunder
by the landowner.
   H.   Lien: In the event that the charges for services are not paid when due
and payable in accordance with the provisions of this chapter, the city clerk-
treasurer or city attorney may make and file a lien against the property within
the time and manner provided for filing liens of mechanics and materialmen
under the provisions of the laws of the state, and such lien shall bind the
premises in the same manner and to the same extent as such mechanics' and
materialmen's liens are binding under the state law, and foreclosed in the same
general manner. Upon foreclosure thereof, attorney fees and costs shall in a
like manner be allowed; or the city may sue to recover the amount due, and for
services provided without such lien or assessment.
   I.   Reconnection Fee: In addition to the foregoing, a mandatory fee of one
hundred dollars ($100.00) shall be charged to the landowner, his heirs,
successors and assigns for restoring services that have been disconnected for
any delinquency regardless of whoever received the benefit of said services, if
anyone. (Ord. 1993-1, 4-8-1993, eff. 4-15-1993)
CHAPTER 5
CROSS CONNECTIONS
SECTION:
10-5-1: Purpose
10-5-2: Definitions
10-5-3: Cross Connections Prohibited
10-5-4: Inspection
10-5-5: Inspection Of Customer's System
10-5-6: Backflow Prevention Device
10-5-7: Liability
10-5-8: Penalty
10-5-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect the public health of water consumers
by the control of actual and/or potential cross connections. (Ord. 1996-2, 3-
14-1996)
10-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
BACKFLOW: The flow other than the intended direction of flow of any foreign
liquids, gases, or substances into the distribution of a public water supply.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE: A device to counteract back pressure or prevent
back siphonage.
CITY: The city of Lava Hot Springs, Idaho, or its authorized agent.
CONTAMINATION: The entry into or presence in a public water supply of any
substance which may be deleterious to health and/or quality of the water.
CROSS CONNECTION: Any physical arrangement whereby a public water supply is
connected, directly or indirectly, with any other water supply system, sewer,
drain, conduit, pool, storage reservoir, plumbing, fixture, or other device
which contains or may contain contaminated water, sewage, or other waste or
liquids of unknown or unsafe quality which may be capable of imparting
contamination to the public water supply as a result of backflow.
CUSTOMER: Any person or persons or other entity using or seeking use of the
municipal water or sewer system of the city.
POTABLE WATER SUPPLY: Any system or water supply intended or used for human
consumption or other domestic uses.
PUBLIC WATER SUPPLY: The city water supply and any main lines, equipment or
appurtenances thereto.
SUPERINTENDENT: The superintendent of public works department, city of Lava Hot
Springs. (Ord. 1996-2, 3-14-1996)
10-5-3: CROSS CONNECTIONS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Installation Or Maintenance Prohibited: The installation or maintenance
of a cross connection which will endanger the water quality of the potable
water supply of the city is prohibited.
   B.   Declared Nuisance: Any such cross connection now existing or hereafter
installed is hereby declared to be a nuisance and shall be abated.
   C.   Compliance Required: The control or elimination of cross connections
shall be in accordance with this chapter and in compliance with Idaho
regulation for public drinking water system 1-8306, or subsequent revision, as
promulgated by the Idaho department of health and welfare. (Ord. 1996-2, 3-14-
1996)
10-5-4: INSPECTION:
   A.   Required Prior To Delivery Of Water: No water shall be delivered to any
structure hereafter built within the city or within areas served by city water
until the same shall have been inspected by the city for possible cross
connections and has been approved as being free of same.
   B.   Backflow Prevention Device Required: Any construction for industrial or
other purposes which is classified as hazardous facilities where it is
reasonable to anticipate intermittent cross connections, or as determined by
the city superintendent, shall be protected by the installation of one or more
backflow prevention device at the point of service from the public water supply
or any other location designated by the city.
   C.   Periodic Inspection: Inspection shall be made periodically by the city
of all buildings, structures or improvements of any kind now receiving water
from the city's system to ascertain whether cross connections exist. (Ord.
1996-2, 3-14-1996)
10-5-5: INSPECTION OF CUSTOMER'S SYSTEM:
The customer's system shall be open for inspection and tests at all reasonable
times to authorized representatives of the city to determine whether cross
connection or other hazards, including violations of these regulations exist.
When such a condition becomes known, the city may deny or immediately
discontinue water service to the premises after providing notice to the
customer until corrections have been rectified in accordance with the state
statute and city ordinances relating to plumbing and water supplies and the
regulations adopted pursuant thereto. (Ord. 1996-2, 3-14-1996)
10-5-6: BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE:
   A.   Required: No water service connected to any premises shall be installed
or maintained by the city unless the water supply is protected as required by
state law and regulation and this chapter. Service of water to any premises may
be discontinued by the city if a backflow prevention device required by this
chapter is not installed, tested and maintained, or it is found that a backflow
prevention device has been removed, bypassed, or if an unprotected cross
connection exists on the premises. Water service shall not be restored until
such conditions are corrected.
   B.   Circumstances Requiring Installation: Backflow prevention devices shall
be installed under circumstances including, but not limited to, the following:
      1.   Premises having an auxiliary water supply;
      2.   Premises having cross connections that are not correctable or
intricate plumbing arrangements which make it impractical to ascertain whether
or not cross connections exist;
      3.   Premises where entry is restricted so that inspections for cross
connections cannot be made with sufficient frequency or at sufficiently short
notice to assure that cross connections do not exist;
      4.   Premises having a history of cross connections being established or
reestablished;
      5.   Premises on which any substance is handled under pressure so as to
permit entry into the public water supply, or where a cross connection could
reasonably be expected to occur. This shall include the handling of process
waters and cooling waters;
      6.   Premises where materials of a toxic or hazardous nature are handled
in such a way that if back siphonage should occur, a serious health hazard
might result;
      7.   The following types of facilities will fall into one of the above
categories where a backflow prevention device is required to protect the public
water supply. A backflow prevention device shall be installed at these
facilities unless the city determines that no hazard exists:
         a.   Agricultural, chemical, storage, formulation and distribution
facilities;
         b.   Animal game farm or zoo;
         c.   Hospitals, mortuaries, clinics;
         d.   Laboratories;
         e.   Metal plating industries;
         f.   Piers and docks;
         g.   Sewage treatment plants;
         h.   Food or beverage processing plants;
         i.   Chemical plants using a water process;
         j.   Petroleum processing or storage plants;
         k.   Radioactive material processing plants or nuclear reactors;
         l.   Tank trucks;
         m.   Fill stations;
         n.   Car washes;
         o.   Wild or exotic animal facility or habitat in which wild animals
are located which are not naturally occurring in the state or are normally
found in the wild;
         p.   Others specified by the city.
   C.   Types Of Devices: The type of protective device required shall depend
on the degree of hazard which exists:
      1.   Health Or System Hazard: An air gap separation or a reduced pressure
principle backflow prevention device shall be installed where the public water
supply may be contaminated with sewage, industrial waste of a toxic nature, or
other contaminant which could cause a health or system hazard.
      2.   Objectionable But Not Hazardous: In the case of a substance which
may be objectionable but not hazardous to health, a double check valve
assembly, air gap separation, or a reduced pressure principle backflow
prevention device shall be installed.
   D.   Cost: The customer shall bear all expense in furnishing and installing
the backflow prevention device.
   E.   Approval Of Device: Any backflow prevention device required by this
chapter shall be approved by the city superintendent prior to installation.
   F.   Location: Where required, an approved backflow prevention device shall
be installed on each service line to a customer's water system at or near the
property line or immediately inside the building being served, but, in all
cases, before the first branch line leading off the service line.
   G.   Supervision Of Installation: Backflow prevention devices required by
this chapter shall be installed under the supervision of the city.
   H.   Annual Inspection: It shall be the duty of the customer at any premises
where backflow prevention devices are installed to have certified inspections
and operational tests made annually. Tests shall be at the expense of the
customer and shall be performed by a state certified tester. These devices
shall be repaired, overhauled or replaced at the expense of the customer
whenever said devices are found to be defective. Records of such tests, repairs
and overhauls shall be kept and copies sent to the city. (Ord. 1996-2, 3-14-
1996)
10-5-7: LIABILITY:
This chapter shall not be construed to hold the city responsible for any damage
to persons or property by reason of the inspection or testing herein, or the
failure to inspect or test, or by reason of approval of any cross connections.
(Ord. 1996-2, 3-14-1996)
10-5-8: PENALTY:
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects, refuses to comply with, or
resists the enforcement of any of the provisions of this chapter or the rules
and regulations as adopted by the city shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor
and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to penalty as provided in
section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 1996-2, 3-14-1996; amd. 2007 Code)
TITLE 11
ZONING REGULATIONS
(Reserved)
TITLE 12
FLOOD CONTROL
CHAPTER 1
FLOOD DAMAGE PREVENTION
SECTION:
12-1-1: Statutory Authorization
12-1-2: Findings Of Fact
12-1-3: Statement Of Purpose
12-1-4: Methods Of Reducing Flood Losses

12-1-12: Violation And Penalties
